  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0eb23b11-eff6-4011-82d8-a1f086073058'
      });
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer13165573035466992533">Rashmirathi (रश्मिरथी), meaning 'the Sun's charioteer', is one of the most popular epic poems of the great Hindi poet, Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar'.   <span id="freeText13165573035466992533" style="display:none">Rashmirathi (रश्मिरथी), meaning 'the Sun's charioteer', is one of the most popular epic poems of the great Hindi poet, Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar'. It is one of the most appreciated works of Dinkar other than "Kurukshetra".<br /><br />Karna was first born son of Kunti whom she had abandoned at birth as he was an illegitimate son. Karna grew up in a lowly family, yet became one of the best warriors of his time. In the Great Mahabharata war, Karna was obliged to fight from the side of Duryodhana as Duryodhana recognizing his merits had made him a king and adopted him as a close friend. Karna fighting from Kaurava's side was a great worry of Pandavas as he was reputed to be unconquerable in war. The way Dinkar has presented the story of Karna with all hues of human emotions trapped in moral dilemmas, is simply marvelous. The rhythm and meter is lilting. Choice of words and purity of language is exhilarating. The work has a timeless relevance and is a must read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13165573035466992533" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<div id="review_183424776" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183424776" />
    <a title="Asra Ghouse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5716249-asra-ghouse"><img alt="Asra Ghouse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434137392p2/5716249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183424776?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Asra Ghouse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Asra Ghouse" href="/user/show/5716249-asra-ghouse">Asra Ghouse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5716249-asra-ghouse?shelf=must-reads">must-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5716249-asra-ghouse?shelf=indian-fiction">indian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183424776" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12702665909929679468">What can one say of Dinkar? Such unequaled is his style!<br/><br/>Rashmirathi is, like how Arundhati Roy puts it in The God of Small Things:<br/><br/><i>"The secret of the Great Stories is that they have no secrets. The Great Stories are the ones you have heard and want to hear again. The ones you can enter anywhere and inhabit comfortably. They don’t deceive you with thrills and trick endings. They don’t surprise you with the unforeseen. They are as familiar as the house you live in. Or the smell of your lover’s skin</i></span>
  <span id="freeText12702665909929679468" style="display:none">What can one say of Dinkar? Such unequaled is his style!<br /><br />Rashmirathi is, like how Arundhati Roy puts it in The God of Small Things:<br /><br /><i>"The secret of the Great Stories is that they have no secrets. The Great Stories are the ones you have heard and want to hear again. The ones you can enter anywhere and inhabit comfortably. They don’t deceive you with thrills and trick endings. They don’t surprise you with the unforeseen. They are as familiar as the house you live in. Or the smell of your lover’s skin. You know how they end, yet you listen as though you don’t. In the way that although you know that one day you will die, you live as though you won’t. In the Great Stories you know who lives, who dies, who finds love, who doesn’t. And yet you want to know again. THAT is their mystery and magic."</i><br /><br />There can be no other way for me to put Rashmirathi's tale. Worth mentioning here is the view Dinkar take on Karna. Ah! Pleasure to the reader (especially to me. Karna is my favourite character!)<br /><br />इस ओर कर्ण मार्तण्ड-सद्रश,<br />उस ओर पार्थ अन्तक-समान<br />रण के मिस, मानो, स्वयं प्रलय,<br />हो उठा समर में मूर्तिमान|<br /><br />The way Dinkar strings up his words, it forms the most precious necklace of verses in the tale. It is like seeing it with your own eyes. For instance,<br /><br />निशा बीती, गगन का रूप दमका,<br />किनारे पर किसी का चीर चमका|<br />क्षितिज के पास लाली छा रही है,<br />अतल से कौन ऊपर आ रही है?<br /><br />Overwhelmed I am, whenever I read Dinkar!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12702665909929679468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12718907551003893096">This book was way beyond my reading level (in Hindi) but despite that, I enjoyed it thoroughly. Reading in Hindi had always felt like a task to me before but this book felt different. It actually made me feel more connected to my language and homeland. <br/><br/>The intrinsic descriptions and the powerful dialogues of Dinkar form an unusually beautiful narrative. I would go so far as to say that Dinkar has super-epified the greatest Indian epic by his rich and insightful writing. What else can I say...</span>

<div id="review_1740403113" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1740403113" />
    <a title="Shishir Chaudhary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4540373-shishir-chaudhary"><img alt="Shishir Chaudhary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489846870p2/4540373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1740403113?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shishir Chaudhary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shishir Chaudhary" href="/user/show/4540373-shishir-chaudhary">Shishir Chaudhary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone who knows Hindi</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4540373-shishir-chaudhary?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1740403113" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11213711872229756541">Whatever you are doing right now, stop, buy this book and read it as early as possible - A one line summary of what this महाकाव्य is and deserves. Many of us have read a small section from this as a part of recommended school reading, the most memorable line being - <br/><br/>जब नाश मनुज पर छाता है<br/>पहले विवेक मर जाता है।<br/>(When the end of a man is nigh,<br/>His common sense is the first to die.)<br/><br/>Composed by one of the greatest Hindi language poets of all times, it is about the most controversial and powerful chara</span>
  <span id="freeText11213711872229756541" style="display:none">Whatever you are doing right now, stop, buy this book and read it as early as possible - A one line summary of what this महाकाव्य is and deserves. Many of us have read a small section from this as a part of recommended school reading, the most memorable line being - <br /><br />जब नाश मनुज पर छाता है<br />पहले विवेक मर जाता है।<br />(When the end of a man is nigh,<br />His common sense is the first to die.)<br /><br />Composed by one of the greatest Hindi language poets of all times, it is about the most controversial and powerful character of Mahabharata - Karna. Composed in वीर रस (Heroic Subgenre), it starts with Duryodhana befriending Karna and ends with Krishna praising Karna after he dies on the battlefield. <br /><br />While this poem turned my perception of Karna upside down, making him the most heroic, honest and mightiest character of the story, it also moved me deeply in some of the sections, bringing me on the brink of shedding tears, especially in two scenes - When Kunti meets Karna a day before the war and when he faces Arjuna's arrows, knowing he was to die unfairly. You have to read it to know what I mean. Apart from the story, Dinkar, throughout, comments on some of the burning issues of today's world - class difference, casteism, war and the idea of victory among many more. For example, following is a stanza in which the poet comments on the impulses of humanity to indulge in wars and compares the current state to the ones of cavemen and species before -<br /><br />झर गयी पूँछ, रोमांत झरे<br />पशुता का झरना बाक़ी है;<br />बाहर-बाहर तन सँवर चुका,<br />मन अभी संवरना बाक़ी है। <br /><br />Strongly recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11213711872229756541" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1028173958" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1508009277468061581">This book is just amazing!!! I got to know about it through facebook since I had liked a few pages on it. I was just enthralled by the lines that were posted from this book. Fortunately I could immediately get it and read it in one stroke. Rashmirathi is the first hindi book I have ever read and probably the best too. I have always been a huge fan of Karna and Mrityunjay and Rashmirathi have deepened my respect and admiration for him. One can read this book over and over and still find it extrem</span>
  <span id="freeText1508009277468061581" style="display:none">This book is just amazing!!! I got to know about it through facebook since I had liked a few pages on it. I was just enthralled by the lines that were posted from this book. Fortunately I could immediately get it and read it in one stroke. Rashmirathi is the first hindi book I have ever read and probably the best too. I have always been a huge fan of Karna and Mrityunjay and Rashmirathi have deepened my respect and admiration for him. One can read this book over and over and still find it extremely fascinating and even more appealing. The best part according to me was the kavach kundal daan. <br /><br />'मैं ही था अपवाद, आज वह भी विभेद हरता हूँ,<br />कवच छोड़ अपना शरीर सबके समान करता हूँ.<br />अच्छा किया कि आप मुझे समतल पर लाने आये,<br />हर तनुत्र दैवीय; मनुज सामान्य बनाने आये. <br /><br />'भुज को छोड़ न मुझे सहारा किसी और सम्बल का,<br />बड़ा भरोसा था, लेकिन, इस कवच और कुण्डल का,<br />पर, उनसे भी आज दूर सम्बन्ध किये लेता हूँ,<br />देवराज! लीजिए खुशी से महादान देता हूँ.<br /> <br />If you can read Hindi just do yourself a favour and read Rashmirathi. The book is a masterpiece in Indian literature. A must read for all the Indian mythology fans.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1508009277468061581" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14172687316135320700">I came across this book after watching this <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cbitu7JXcrM' rel='nofollow noopener'>video</a>, in which Manoj Bajpai beautifully recites verses from one of the chapters of Rashmirathi. The book eulogizes Karna, who is well-known not just for his skills and prowess as a warrior but also for his generosity and unrelenting pursuit of <i>Dharma</i>.<br/>Recite it. Each verse is filled with rhythmic music and will leave you delighted.</span>
  <span id="freeText14172687316135320700" style="display:none">I came across this book after watching this <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Cbitu7JXcrM" rel="nofollow noopener">video</a>, in which Manoj Bajpai beautifully recites verses from one of the chapters of Rashmirathi. The book eulogizes Karna, who is well-known not just for his skills and prowess as a warrior but also for his generosity and unrelenting pursuit of <i>Dharma</i>.<br />Recite it. Each verse is filled with rhythmic music and will leave you delighted.</span>

  <span id="freeText10880122416185966049" style="display:none">I would not take the credit off from Piyush mishra for popularizing the parts of this epos. if you have not seen gulal as well, it is the chapter where Krishna goes to duryodhan and asks rajya for the pandavas and on the refusal of duryodhan gets angry and challanges him for the battle. This chapter beautifully captures the aggravated emotions of the otherwise tactical Krishna and the fear he inculcates in the Sabha.<br /> <br />well thats with the popularised chapter but the rest of it is equally historical and grande. the chapters on Karn, his trainig wirh parshuram, Krishna's negotiations with Karn etc .. everything about this epos is Hitorical. So if you can read in Hindi, this is a must. Please do read this in Hindi and not any english translations and explanations. To say the least its like reading Kafka in German :) (which i cannot). <br /><br />Cheers!!</span>

<div id="review_1782293350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1782293350" />
    <a title="Vikalp Trivedi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39776026-vikalp-trivedi"><img alt="Vikalp Trivedi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433140916p2/39776026.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1782293350?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vikalp Trivedi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vikalp Trivedi" href="/user/show/39776026-vikalp-trivedi">Vikalp Trivedi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39776026-vikalp-trivedi?shelf=reading-challenge-2016">reading-challenge-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1782293350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12530532128299626556">"Rashmirathi" by Ramdhari Singh Dinkar is a phenomenal poem based on the life and moreover struggle of the most underrated character of the Mahabharat - Karn . The poem is composed in Veer-Ras and is composed so brilliantly that it literally gives goosebumps to the reader .<br/><br/>I've read some books based on the Mahabharata in which Karn is one of the chief character . But those books mostly portrayed the tragidies surrounding Karn's life and on the other hand this books portrays the stand of Karn aga</span>
  <span id="freeText12530532128299626556" style="display:none">"Rashmirathi" by Ramdhari Singh Dinkar is a phenomenal poem based on the life and moreover struggle of the most underrated character of the Mahabharat - Karn . The poem is composed in Veer-Ras and is composed so brilliantly that it literally gives goosebumps to the reader .<br /><br />I've read some books based on the Mahabharata in which Karn is one of the chief character . But those books mostly portrayed the tragidies surrounding Karn's life and on the other hand this books portrays the stand of Karn against all the odds he faced throughout his life . Entire poem was great but the parts I liked most were the training days of Karn with Parshuram (especially Parshuram's affection for Karn) , conversation of Karn with Krishna , Indra and Kunti and Krishna's warning in the Kuru Court . It happens with every book related to the Mahabharat that it gives many answers to many questions , but also asks some new ones . This book is no exception and it poses some questions on the Pandav side which should be thought of and also there are the ones which directly questions their agenda itself of fighting the war .<br /><br />There is one more thing which I liked about the poem that the author has used many incedences of the Mahabharata to target the condition of the nation at the time "Rashmirathi" was published (mainly caste discrimination and evils of war) ironically many of the conditions are still the same . <br /><br />Overall a wonderful and intriguing book.<br />Perfect 5 Stars.<br /><br />P.S. - The book marks my 50th read book on Goodreads . Glad it was my 50th book .</span>
  <a data-text-id="12530532128299626556" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2071384310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2071384310" />
    <a title="Shubham Joshi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50728081-shubham-joshi"><img alt="Shubham Joshi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501229029p2/50728081.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2071384310?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shubham Joshi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shubham Joshi" href="/user/show/50728081-shubham-joshi">Shubham Joshi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2071384310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14304834498450170694">'Rashmirathi' or 'The Sun's Charioteer' is an epic Hindi poem based on the story of Karna, a pivotal character in the Hindu epic Mahabharata.<br/><br/>Penned by Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar', the national poet of the country, Rashmirathi is a Maha-Katha-Kavya, a poem that tells a philosophically dense and psychologically engaging story in a lyrical fashion.<br/><br/>Dinkar was a champion of the 'Veer Ras'; a poetic flavor that prioritizes struggle/war as a necessary ingredient of a person's success.<br/><br/>The entirety of the po</span>
  <span id="freeText14304834498450170694" style="display:none">'Rashmirathi' or 'The Sun's Charioteer' is an epic Hindi poem based on the story of Karna, a pivotal character in the Hindu epic Mahabharata.<br /><br />Penned by Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar', the national poet of the country, Rashmirathi is a Maha-Katha-Kavya, a poem that tells a philosophically dense and psychologically engaging story in a lyrical fashion.<br /><br />Dinkar was a champion of the 'Veer Ras'; a poetic flavor that prioritizes struggle/war as a necessary ingredient of a person's success.<br /><br />The entirety of the poem is about the Surya-Putra Karna, who was conceived by Kunti(Mother of Pandvas) via the Sun God before her marriage to Pandu. Ashamed of the premarital birth of her son, she abandons Karna in a basket and lets him drift away.<br /><br />Karna pays the price of someone else's actions, as he would do throughout his life.<br />Karna was then found by a low caste 'Sut' (Stableman) who raises him as his son.<br />The tragic separation of Karna from his own mother, in which his mother alone was alone to be blamed is captured beautifully by Dinkar. Dinkar says that those who wish to win the world, will win it regardless of anythting but their own grit, struggle and valor.<br /><br />जिसके पिता सूर्य थे, माता कुन्ती सती कुमारी, (His father was Surya, mother was Kunti<br />उसका पलना हुई धार पर बहती हुई पिटारी। (He who was raised in a basket floating in the river)<br />सूत-वंश में पला, चखा भी नहीं जननि का क्षीर, (Raised in a lowly caste,never tasted her mother's milk)<br />निकला कर्ण सभी युवकों में तब भी अद्भुत वीर। ( Despite this, Karna came out to be unconquerable)<br /><br />Karna's hatred for Arjuna is very well known. But why ?<br /><br />Arjuna was everything that Karna was and wasn't.<br />Karna was as skillful as Arjuna, an even-better archer. But Karna didn't enjoy the same privileges as Arjuna did.<br />Arjuna was a prince, a Kshatriya, had a skillful teacher by his side and enjoyed the applause and approval of the crowd.<br /><br />To subvert the situation, Karna openly challenges Arjuna in tourney organised by Dronacharya(Arjuna's Guru). His battle cry and call-out to Arjuna to accept his challenge is again beautifully captured.<br /><br />"तालियों से क्या रहा गर्व में फूल ?<br />अर्जुन ! तेरा सुयश अभी क्षण में होता है धूल।<br /><br />तूने जो-जो किया, उसे मैं भी दिखला सकता हूँ,<br />चाहे तो कुछ नयी कलाएँ भी सिख़ला सकता हूँ।<br />आँख खोलकर देख, कर्ण के हाथों का व्यापार,<br />फूले सस्ता सुयश प्राप्त कर, उस नर को धिक्कार।" <br /><br />Despite his bravery, he isn't allowed to fight and is asked his caste. He again replies in Dinkar's tearing words-<br /><br />‘जाति ! हाय री जाति !’ कर्ण का हृदय क्षोभ से डोला,<br />कुपित सूर्य की ओर देख वह वीर क्रोध से बोला-<br />‘‘जाति-जाति रटते, जिनकी पूँजी केवल पाषण्ड,<br />मैं क्या जानूँ जाति ? जाति हैं ये मेरे भुजदण्ड।<br /><br />‘‘ऊपर सिर पर कनक-छत्र, भीतर काले-के-काले,<br />शरमाते हैं नहीं जगत् में जाति पूछनेवाले।<br />सूतपुत्र हूँ मैं, लेकिन, थे पिता पार्थ के कौन ?<br />साहस हो तो कहो, ग्लानि से रह जाओ मत मौन।<br /><br />‘‘मस्तक ऊँचा किये, जाति का नाम लिये चलते हो,<br />पर, अधर्ममय शोषण के बल से सुख में पलते हो।<br />अधम जातियों से थर-थर काँपते तुम्हारे प्राण,<br />छल से माँग लिया करते हो अँगूठे का दान।<br /><br />‘‘पूछो मेरी जाति, शक्ति हो तो, मेरे भुजबल से,<br />रवि-समान दीपित ललाट से, और कवच-कुण्डल से।<br />पढ़ो उसे जो झलक रहा है मुझमें तेज-प्रकाश,<br />मेरे रोम-रोम में अंकित है मेरा इतिहास।<br /><br />‘‘अर्जुन बड़ा वीर क्षत्रिय है तो आगे वह आवे,<br />क्षत्रियत्व का तेज जरा मुझको भी तो दिखलावे।<br />अभी छीन इस राजपुत्र के कर से तीर-कमान,<br />अपनी महाजाति की दूँगा मैं तुमको पहचान।<br /><br />The entire poem is an immersive leap into Karna's lfe. And Ramdhari says that Karna hasn't died.<br />There are several Karnas born today, who are skillful and hardworking and yet are not allowed to hold positions because of their caste,sex or race.<br /><br />When Karna is asked what will his legacy be, he says in unbearable fashion that brings tears to my eyes -<br /><br />मैं उनका आदर्श, कहीं जो व्यथा न खोल सकेंगे,<br />पूछेगा जग, किन्तु पिता का नाम न बोल सकेंगे;<br />जिनका निखिल विश्व में कोई कहीं न अपना होगा,<br />मन में लिये उमंग जिन्हें चिर-काल कलपना होगा।<br /><br />Ramdhari Singh was a talismanic poet,his words will make you question everything around you and at the same time give you the strength to bear the ills of society for others, and fight them.<br /><br />A poet completely on par with W.B.Yeats, Pushkin and Keats, if not better.<br /><br />The poem is a treasure of modern Hindi literature and Dinkar its pioneer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14304834498450170694" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3300162716" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3300162716" />
    <a title="Ayushi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30986781-ayushi"><img alt="Ayushi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464935544p2/30986781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3300162716?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ayushi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ayushi" href="/user/show/30986781-ayushi">Ayushi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3300162716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15041714471612752709">One of the greatest masterpieces of Hindi literature, Rashmirathi centers around the life, struggle and death of one of the most popular Mahabharata characters, Karna. I had read a small part of this epic poem as part of the required reading in high school. The rhythm and choice of words are unparalleled and create a beautiful visual in front of the reader’s eyes. I would recommend reading this in the original Hindi version. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText8531799766511538642" style="display:none">This is one of the best pieces of poetry I have read in a while. I read the original version in Hindi. For a long time, I had ignored this book thinking of it as just another story of Karna. But I was so wrong. It highlights so many different colors that paint a human life. Through a captivating description of various incidents in Mahabharata mainly centered around Karna's life, the poet Dinkarji goes on to talk about honor, love, destiny and about the depths to which human characters fall in the course of a war. I can totally see why so many people, commoners and celebs alike, say that this book gave them hope and inspired them in the difficult times of their lives. </span>

    <a title="Farozan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55350579-farozan"><img alt="Farozan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469627579p2/55350579.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_3318557956" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3318557956" />
    <a title="Tanay Raj" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112034285-tanay-raj"><img alt="Tanay Raj" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3318557956?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tanay Raj" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tanay Raj" href="/user/show/112034285-tanay-raj">Tanay Raj</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3318557956&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3318557956" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6751874581296867182">Rashmirathi is among the greatest works of one of most eminent poets of Hindi Romanticism. As the name suggests, the epic poem talks about the life and struggles of Karna, one of the major characters of Mahabharata. The life of Karna is the most tragic among the characters of Mahabharata and has been the subject or several literary works. Born to Princess Kunti before her marriage, Karna was abandoned at birth and was raised in a lower caste household. He is, again and again, reminded of his low</span>
  <span id="freeText6751874581296867182" style="display:none">Rashmirathi is among the greatest works of one of most eminent poets of Hindi Romanticism. As the name suggests, the epic poem talks about the life and struggles of Karna, one of the major characters of Mahabharata. The life of Karna is the most tragic among the characters of Mahabharata and has been the subject or several literary works. Born to Princess Kunti before her marriage, Karna was abandoned at birth and was raised in a lower caste household. He is, again and again, reminded of his lower caste identity, ridiculed, and humiliated. Even then, Karna emerges as one of the bravest and most righteous warriors ever known, even capable of besting the Pandavas, and even more righteous than Krishna himself.<br />The entire poem is divided into seven parts, with each part consisting, usually, of a dialogue between Karna and another of the Epic's major character. The dialogue between Karna and Kunti, and Krishna's warning to Duryodhan are well known excerpts, which are of philosophical interest in their own right. Each dialogue is replete with deep ethical questions and moral dilemmas, and ends with the other character submitting to Karma's stature as a man of honour, bravery and righteousness, who, despite having been wronged by destiny time and again, holds on to these very values that define him. Not to mention, Dinkar's verse with skillful and persistent use of onomatopoeia and alliteration starkly brings out the emotions underlying the characters' state of mind. <br />Finally, what makes this piece stand apart relative to other known works surrounding the Hindu epics, is Dinkar's use of the instances in Mahabharata as allegories to casteism, hypocrisy, and even falseness of Gods, which is not only an evidence of the greatness of the epic Mahabharata but also tells us why the 3000 year old epic is still relevant.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6751874581296867182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3373828161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3373828161" />
    <a title="Atulit Singh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76248759-atulit-singh"><img alt="Atulit Singh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566986920p2/76248759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3373828161?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Atulit Singh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Atulit Singh" href="/user/show/76248759-atulit-singh">Atulit Singh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3373828161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5335208042051906042">What perspective! Karna has always been my favorite character among all the major ones in Mahabharata. Rashmirathi is pristine poetry about Karna's character (well, mostly) and in general a question slammed onto the face of dharma by Dinkar ji. I had been reading a few stanzas bit by bit on a near daily basis for the past 3 months. It was just so much to take in, so much to reflect upon, that even 5 stanzas at a time sometimes seemed like a difficult task. Hindi is my mother tongue, but I had ne</span>
  <span id="freeText5335208042051906042" style="display:none">What perspective! Karna has always been my favorite character among all the major ones in Mahabharata. Rashmirathi is pristine poetry about Karna's character (well, mostly) and in general a question slammed onto the face of dharma by Dinkar ji. I had been reading a few stanzas bit by bit on a near daily basis for the past 3 months. It was just so much to take in, so much to reflect upon, that even 5 stanzas at a time sometimes seemed like a difficult task. Hindi is my mother tongue, but I had never really read any poetry in the language. In other words, this was my first Hindi poem. I have been absolutely delighted and at moments moved to tears by Dinkar Ji, through the rhythm that he installs in between the lines (and which will be lost in translation to any other language), so much so that I read Pratham Sarg and Tritiya Sarga (my favourites) so many times that I can literally recite every line in order from memory, which is like around 100 stanzas. Absolutely loved it. So inspirational!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5335208042051906042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ErUlAGOf4X7vlPy+Chtz+jBBTyJNWlGUwEqxI80G/6PNS5E7ERO8S6X4ymA2e5bLbOoSHDkdcsB/T9I2jN8xVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cL9YH1qjgfQ9XU26elt8h47heaP//VP/et9YfrxOFxOvQewkKC/cwXcxe2RGO5m20koknYu6cKvF2jtr/ZfZ5Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

It is considered one of the greatest literary works written in modern times in Hindi literature. It also signifies the epitome of Chhayavadi school of<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11454925238698994199\" style=\"display:none\">Kamayani (Hindi:कामायनी) (1936) is a Hindi epic poem (Mahakavya) by Jaishankar Prasad (1889- 1937). It is considered one of the greatest literary works written in modern times in Hindi literature. It also signifies the epitome of Chhayavadi school of Hindi poetry which gained popularity in late nineteenth and early twentieth century.\n\nKamayani depicts the interplay of human emotions, thoughts, and actions by taking mythological metaphors. Kamayani has personalities like Manu, Ida and Shraddha who are found in the Vedas. The great deluge described in the poem has its origin in Satapatha Brahmana. Explaining his metaphorical presentation of Vedic characters, the poet said:\n&quot;Ida was the sister of the gods, giving consciousness to entire mankind. For this reason there is an Ida Karma in the Yagnas. This erudition of Ida created a rift between Shraddha and Manu. Then with the progressive intelligence searching for unbridled pleasures, the impasse was inevitable. This story is so very ancient that metaphor has wonderfully mingled with history. Therefore, Manu, Shraddha and Ida while maintaining their historical importance may also express the symbolic import. Manu represents the mind with its faculties of the head and heart and these are again symbolized as Faith (Shraddha) and Intelligence (Ida) respectively. On this data is based the story of Kamayani.&quot;\nThe plot is based on the Vedic story where Manu, the man surviving after the deluge (Pralaya), is emotionless (Bhavanasunya). Manu starts getting involved in various emotions, thoughts and actions. These are sequentially portrayed with Shraddha, Ida, Kilaat and other characters playing there part, contributing in them. The chapters are named after these emotions, thoughts or actions. Some people consider that the sequence of chapters denotes the change of personality in a mans life with age.\nFollowing is the sequence:\n\nChinta (Anxiety)\nAsha (Hope)\nShraddha (Reverential belief, Faith, Virtue of being a woman)\nKama (Sexual love)\nVasna (Passion for material pleasure)\nLajja (Shyness)\nKarma (Action)\nIrshyaa (Jealousy)\nIda (Logic, Intellect)\nSwapna (Dream)\nSangharsh (Internal conflict)\nNirved (Disregard of worldly things, Renunciation)\nDarshan (Philosophy, Vision)\nRahasya (Hidden knowledge, Mystery)\nAnand (Bliss, Self-realization, Shiva)<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11454925238698994199\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13510351.Ramdhari_Singh_Dinkar_">About Ramdhari Singh &#39;Dinkar&#39;</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/13510351.Ramdhari_Singh_Dinkar_"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1431410969p3/13510351.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/13510351.Ramdhari_Singh_Dinkar_">Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar'
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3066477687735591983">Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar' (September 23, 1908 – April 24, 1974) was an Indian Hindi poet, essayist, patriot and academic,[1][2] who is considered as one of the most important modern Hindi poets. He remerged as a poet of rebellion as a consequence of his nationalist poetry written in the days before Indian independence. His poetry exuded veer rasa, and he has been hailed as a Rashtrakavi ("National p</span>
  <span id="freeText3066477687735591983" style="display:none">Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar' (September 23, 1908 – April 24, 1974) was an Indian Hindi poet, essayist, patriot and academic,[1][2] who is considered as one of the most important modern Hindi poets. He remerged as a poet of rebellion as a consequence of his nationalist poetry written in the days before Indian independence. His poetry exuded veer rasa, and he has been hailed as a Rashtrakavi ("National poet") on account of his inspiring patriotic compositions.[3]<br /><br />As a mark of respect for him, his portrait was unveiled in the Central Hall of Parliament of India by the Prime Minister of India, Dr. Manmohan Singh on his centenary year, 2008.[4][5] On 23 November 2012, the President of India, Pranab Mukherjee gave away Rashtrakavi Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar' Sahitya Ratna Samman to 21 prominent writers and social workers at a function organized in Rashtrapati Bhavan.[6] On the occasion, the President recalled the contribution of Ramdhari Singh 'Dinkar' in the freedom struggle and his service to Hindi literature.[6] Poet and former Prime Minister of India, Atal Bihari Vajpayee spoke of Dinkarji in high esteem.[7] Others who have praised his literary genius include Shivraj Patil, Lal Krishna Advani, Somnath Chatterjee, Gulab Khandelwal, Bhawani Prasad Mishra, and Seth Govind Das.[8]<br /><br />Dinkar initially supported the revolutionary movement during the Indian independence struggle, but later became a Gandhian. However, he used to call himself a 'Bad Gandhian' because he supported the feelings of indignation and revenge among the youth.[9] In Kurukshetra, he accepted that war is destructive but argued that it is necessary for the protection of freedom. He was close to prominent nationalists of the time such as Rajendra Prasad, Anugrah Narayan Sinha, Sri Krishna Sinha, Rambriksh Benipuri and Braj Kishore Prasad.<br /><br />Dinkar was elected three times to the Rajya Sabha, and he was the member of this house from April 3, 1952 CE to January 26, 1964 CE,[9] and was awarded the Padma Bhushan in 1959.[9] He was also the Vice Chancellor of Bhagalpur University (Bhagalpur, Bihar) in the early 1960s.<br /><br />During The Emergency, Jayaprakash Narayan had attracted a gathering of one lakh people at the Ramlila grounds and recited Dinkar's famous poem: Singhasan Khaali Karo Ke Janata Aaati Hai (Devanagari: सिंहासन खाली करो कि जनता आती है; "Vacate the throne, for the people come").[10]</span>
  <a data-text-id="3066477687735591983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;दो न्याय अगर तो आधा दो,<br /><br />पर, इसमें भी यदि बाधा हो,<br />तो दे दो केवल पाँच ग्राम,<br /><br />रक्खो अपनी धरती तमाम।<br />हम वहीं खुशी से खायेंगे,<br /><br />परिजन पर असि न उठायेंगे!<br /><br /><br />दुर्योधन वह भी दे ना सका,<br /><br />आशिष समाज की ले न सका,<br />उलटे, हरि को बाँधने चला,<br /><br />जो था असाध्य, साधने चला।<br />जन नाश मनुज पर छाता है,<br /><br />पहले विवेक मर जाता है।<br /><br /><br />हरि ने भीषण हुंकार किया,<br /><br />अपना स्वरूप-विस्तार किया,<br />डगमग-डगमग दिग्गज डोले,<br /><br />भगवान् कुपित होकर बोले-<br />'जंजीर बढ़ा कर साध मुझे,<br /><br />हाँ, हाँ दुर्योधन! बाँध मुझे।<br /><br /><br />यह देख, गगन मुझमें लय है,<br /><br />यह देख, पवन मुझमें लय है,<br />मुझमें विलीन झंकार सकल,<br /><br />मुझमें लय है संसार सकल।<br />अमरत्व फूलता है मुझमें,<br /><br />संहार झूलता है मुझमें।&rdquo;</span>
